@001\
INTRODUCTION\
The da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mikas\u363 tra occupies a position of paramount importance\
in the mah\uc0\u257 y\u257 na system of thought.It also goes under the name of\
da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mika\u347 dastra, da\u347 abh\u363 mi\u347 vara and the like. \u257 c\u257 rya asa\u7749 ga in\
his da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mihas referred to it by the name of da\u347 abh\u363 maka.It is\
remarkable evidence of its supreme authority and immense popularity\
that it has been translated into the Tibetan, Chinese, Japanese, Mangolian \
and other languages.A detailed account of the different manuscripts and\
versions of the da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mikas\u363 tra has been furnished by Dr.Johannes \
Rahder in his illuminating preface to it.The g\uc0\u257 th\u257 s occurring in the \
last chapter are conspicuous by their absence in the earlier manuscripts\
of it.And this fact has induced a section of scholars of mah\uc0\u257 y\u257 na\
buddhism to dub them as inter addenda.The two the laligavistara\
graphies of the Buddha, viz.the mah\uc0\u257 vastu and the Lalitavistara\
have referred to the different stages in the spiritual career of the Bodhi-\
sattava and the means of their realization.Besides there are innume-\
rable mah\uc0\u257 y\u257 na texts that have made a comprehensive treatment of \
them in their own independent way.The lock of their concurrence \
concerning the conception of the different Bodhisattava-stages is too \
obvious to require an elaboration.A few eminent scholars have made \
a sedulous attaempt to discover correspondence among the different \
stages expounded by different mah\uc0\u257 y\u257 nist  theologians.It merits mention\
that the h\uc0\u299 nay\u257 nist differs from the mah\u257 y\u257 nist on the underlying \
symbolism and mysticism of the bodhisattava-bh\uc0\u363 mis.\
The present text of the da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mika-s\u363 tra has been prepared by\
Dr.P.L.Vaidya, former Director of the Mithila Research Institute,\
on the basis of Johannes Rahder\'92s edition.And since the edition\
princeps is out of print, a fresh publication of this important classic\
is expected to meet a genuine dcsideratum in the study of\
mah\uc0\u257 y\u257 na cultus.\
The text of the da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mika-s\u363 tra abounds in sesquipedalian\
phraseology and gorgeous metaphor.So a serious study of this work \
is bound to Strain the patience of an average student of mah\uc0\u257 y\u257 na\
literature.We have, however, presented a brief and faithful survey of \
the ten bodhisattava-bh\uc0\u363 mis with special emphasis on their salient features.\
1.The pramudit\uc0\u257 \
A future Bodhisattava prepares himself to undertake a long and \
strenuous journey for the realization of Bodhisattavahood.He concen-\
@002\
trates on his mental, intellectual, and spiritual edification.On the eve\
of his departure, the thought of enlightenment is awakened (bodhicittaot-\
p\uc0\u257 da)\{1.This technical term is susceptioble of different interpretations.\} \
in his mind due to the immaculacy of his dispositions and trans-\
parency of his inward resolution.Consequently he aspires after the \
attainment of buddha-knowledge, ten powers, deliverance of the whole \
world and other supreme qualities.His aspiration for the realization of \
the ultimate goal of bodhisattavahood impels him to the ceaseless \
pursuit of it.He reaches the first stage in the spiritual career of the \
bodhisattava and it passes under the name of pramudit\uc0\u257 .It is so-called \
because supreme delight permcates this stage.\{2.Cf. pa\uc0\u347 yat\u257  bodhim \u257 sann\u257 \u7747  sattav\u257 rthasya ca s\u257 dhanam| tivra \
utpadyate modo mudit\uc0\u257  tena kathyate || s\u363 tr\u257 l.XXI32.\} He takes refuge in \
perfect enlightenment (sa\uc0\u7747 bodhipar\u257 ya\u7751 a).He brings his passions under \
subjection.He becomes exempt from five terrors, viz.(1) terror per-\
taining to means of livelihood, (2) to blame, (3) to death, (4) to evil\
destiny, and (5) to timorousness in an assembly.\{3.The following arguments have been act forth in order to account for the \
disappearance of terror adverted to above yad idam \uc0\u257 jivak\u257 bhaya\u7747  v\u257  \

bhaya\uc0\u7747  v\u257 , t\u257 ni sarv\u257 \u7751 i vyapagat\u257 ni bhavanti.tatkasya heto: ? yath\u257 \'92pi \
idam \uc0\u257 tmasa\u7747 j\'f1\u257 pagam\u257 d \u257 tmasncho\'92 sya na bhavati, kuta: puna:\
sarvopakara\uc0\u7751 asneha: ? atosya \u257 j\u299 vik\u257 bhaya\u7747  na bhavati.na ca \
kai\uc0\u7747 cit satk\u257 ra\u7747  kasyacit sak\u257 \u347 \u257 t pratik\u257 \u7749 k\u7779 ati, anyatra mayaiva\
te\uc0\u7779 \u257 \u7747  sattav\u257 n\u257 \u7747  sarvopakara\u7751 ah\u257 bulyam\'85, ato\'92sya a\u347 lokabhaya\u7747  \
na bhavati.\uc0\u257 tmad\u7771 \u7779 \u7789 ivigam\u257 c ca a\u347 y\u257 tnasa\u7747 j\'f1\u257  na bhavati.ato\'92sya \

ch\uc0\u257 radyabhaya\u7747  na bhavati-DBHS, 9.\} He becomes atteneded \
with the different purifying virtues intended for the purification of the \
bodhisattava-bh\uc0\u363 mi.\
A Bodhisattava-to-be who abides in this stage makes the following \
ten great pra\uc0\u7751 idh\u257 nas \{4.The mah\u257 y\u257 na texts have provided an exhaustive list of the different types \
of bodhisattava\'92s  pra\uc0\u7751 idh\u257 na.But the lack of unanimity among them is \
too pronounced to call for an clucidation.It is usually held that the \

A Bodhisattava firmly established in this pramudit\uc0\u257 -bh\u363 mi gains \
sovereignty over  jambudv\uc0\u299 pa.His activities are, viz. charity (d\u257 na),\
@005\
(2) speaking in a pleasing way (priyavadyat\uc0\u257 ), (3) rendering good to \
others (arthakriy\uc0\u257 ), (4) pursuing identical religious goals with others \
(sam\uc0\u257 n\u257 rthat\u257 \{1.Cf.four sa\u7747 graha-vastus.\}  who are not excluded from or averse to the mental \
reflection on the Buddha, the Doctrine (dharma), sa\uc0\u7747 gha, and so \
forth and so on.He earnestly desires to become the first, foremost,\
and best of all beings.He sets his energy in motion in conformity \
with his aspirations.As a result of it, he renounces his worldly \
belongings and adopts the religious instruction of the Buddha as a \
wandering monk.This enables him to attain one hundred mystic \
trances in one moment, to behold one hundred Buddhas and to know \
their adhis\uc0\u7789 h\u257 nas; to shake and illuminate one hundred world-orders;\
to bring one hundred creatures to maturity; to remain for one hundred \
kalpas; to enter into one hundred kalpas in the past and the future; \
to discriminate one hundred doors (entrances, mukha) of dharma; to \
exhibit one hundred magically created bodies; to show each and \
every individual body accompanied by a retinue of one hundred \
Bodhisattvas.\{2.The da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mika-s\u363 tra has rciterated that a bodhisattva gains mastery \
of innumerable magic powers in each stage of his spiritual career.\} \
2.The vimal\uc0\u257 \
A candidate for the ideal status of the bodhisattva brings his \
spiritual preparation to a high level of perfection in the first stage.\
He continues his journey with burning faith and fervour.He succeeds \
in reaching the second stage which is called vimal\uc0\u257  inasmuch as it is \
exempt from dross or defilement.It is in this stage that his ten mental \
dispositions \{3.The da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mika-s\u363 tra, 15 has made the following pertinent obacrvation: \

He becomes provided with ten good courses of action \{4.......da\uc0\u347 abhi: ku\u347 alai: karmapathai: samanv\u257 gato bhavati-DBHS, 15.\} which may be\
classified in the following order: (1) three physical viz.abstention\
from taking life (pr\uc0\u257 \u7751 atip\u257 t\u257 t prativirata:), theft (adatt\u257 d\u257 n\u257 t-), and sinful \
sexual relation (k\uc0\u257 ma-mithy\u257 c\u257 r\u257 t-); (2) four vocal, viz.abstention\
@006\
from speech which is false (an\uc0\u7771 tavacan\u257 t prativirata:), spiteful (pi\u347 -\
uavacan\uc0\u257 t-), har\u7779 a (paru\u7779 avacan\u257 t-), and confused or nonsensical\

ousnes (an\uc0\u257 abhidhy\u257 lu), from malice (avy\u257 pann\u257 citta), and from evil\
heretical view (kud\uc0\u7771 \u7779 \u7789 i).He did not attain this physical, vocal and\
mental purity in the previous stage.\
He preserves these ten good courses of action and effectuates\
gradual elevation of his mental dispositions.\{1.DBHS, 15-6\} He understands that it \
is not possible for him to establish others in good conduct (behavior,\
pratipatti), while he himself remains in an evil one.He becomes\
aware of the fact that the initial stages in the purification\
of the ten good courses of action are conducive to the attainment of \
the vehicles of \uc0\u347 r\u257 vakas and pratyekabuddhas.But the successive\
stages, lead to the rarefication of the boddhisattva-bh\uc0\u363 mi and virtues\
of perfection, and the development of the course of good conduct.And\
yet the following moreand more refined stages eventuate in the \
attainment of ten powers and the like.\{2.Ibid.\} It becomes revealed to him \
that all the saints should practice the Yoga for the effectuation of ourifi-\
cation of all froms.\{3.\'85sarv\uc0\u257 k\u257 rapari\u347 odhan\u257 bhinirh\u257 ra eva yoga: kara\u7751 \u299 ya: \'85Ibid.\}\
He ponders over the deplorable consequences that are entailed\
by the adoption of ten evil courses of action (da\uc0\u347 a-aku\u347 \u257 la-karmapatha).\
The more he reflect upon the moral, intellectual and spiritual deterio-\
ration of the deserters of the ten good paths, the more he realizes\
their precarious predicament. He is not a mere mute spectator\
of their trials and tribulations.He is overpowered with boundless\
love and compassion for all sentient beings hurled in to the bottomless \
barathrum of sorrows and sufferings.He becomes conscious of his \
bounden duty to reclaim those renegades from the ten paths of \
violence and corruption.He begins to feel that it is incumbent upon \
him to install them in the stage of nirv\uc0\u257 \u7751 a and in the great vehicle.\
He knows that nirv\uc0\u257 \u7751 a is of the nature of supreme bliss inasmuch as \
it involves the extinction of the five skandhas, the basis of ego-centric\
personality and the consequent misery of metempsychosis.\{4.\'85te\'92sm\uc0\u257 bhi: paramasukhe sarvaniketavigame prati\u7779 \u7789 h\u257 payitavy\u257  yad\
uta\'85nirv\uc0\u257 \u7751 e- DBHS, 18.\}\
@007\
A Bodhisattva who dwells in this immaculate stage realizes \
that innumerable Buddhas have come into the field of his vision.He \
arrives at purity of renunciation and perfection of morality.He\
attains the primacy of the quality of speaking in a leving manner\
(priyavadyat\uc0\u257 ) and moral perfection (\u347 \u299 lap\u257 ramit\u257 ) in this realm.\{1.tasya caturabhya: sa\u7747 grahavastubhya: priyavadyat\u257  atiriktatam\u257  bhavati.\
da\uc0\u347 abhya: p\u257 ramit\u257 bhya: \u347 \u299 lap\u257 ramit\u257  atiriktatam\u257  bhavati- DBHS,18.\} He \
becomes the supreme lord of the four island and provided with\
seven jewels.\
3.The prabh\uc0\u257 kari\
A future Bodhisattva pursues his spiritual career and ascends \
the third stage called prabh\uc0\u257 kari or the Illuminating. \{2.mah\u257 dharm\u257 vabh\u257 sasya kara\u7751 \u257 c ca prabh\u257 par\u299  s\u363 tr\u257 l, XXI.33\} He treads on it \
accompanied by (ten) mental concentrations (manask\uc0\u257 ra) on ten mental \
disposition (citt\uc0\u257 \u347 aya), viz.(1) on pure mental disposition, (2) on \
steadfast mental disposition, (3) on dispassionate mental disposition,\
(4) on non-dispassionate mental disposition, (5) on non-recurring mental \
disposition (6) on firm and obdurate mental disposition, and the \
like \{3....da\uc0\u347 abhi\u347  citt\u257 \u347 ayamanask\u257 rair \u257 kramati.katamair da\u347 abhi: ? yad\
uta \uc0\u347 uddhacitt\u257 \u347 yamanask\u257 re\u7751 a ca sthiracitt\u257 \u347 ayamanask\u257 re\u7751 a ca nir-\
viccitt\uc0\u257 \u347 ayamanask\u257 re\u7751 a ca avir\u257 gacitt\u257 \u347 ayamanask\u257 re\u7751 a ca avinivarta-\
citt\uc0\u257 sayamanask\u257 re\u7751 a ca d\u7771 \u7693 hacittasayamanask\u257 re\u7751 a ca, uttaptacitt\u257 \u347 aya-\
manask\uc0\u257 re\u7751 a ca, at\u7771 ptacitt\u257 \u347 ayamanask\u257 re\u7751 a ca... et seq, DBHS, 19.\} He thoroughly reflects on the fact that all conditioned states of \
being (thing, sa\uc0\u7747 sk\u257 ra) are impermanent, painful, inauspicious, unde-\
pendable, and suseptible to production and annihilation in a moment.\
Furthermore, they are not liable to revert to the past, not liaable to pass\
into another state in the future, and not liable to discrimination in the \
present.\{4.\'85anityat\uc0\u257 \u7747  ca sarvasa\u7747 sk\u257 ragatasya yath\u257 bh\u363 ta\u7747  prabhuta\u7747  pratyavek\u7779 ate, \
du:khat\uc0\u257 \u7747  ca a\u347 ubhat\u257 \u7747  ca an\u257 \u347 v\u257 sikat\u257 \u7747  ca vipralopat\u257 \u7747  ca acirasthi-\

mind in motion and direct it towards tath\uc0\u257 gata-knowledge.Gradually\
he becomes conscious of its numerous rare qualities including its\
conduciveness to deliverance of innumerable individuals.He com-\
@008\
prehends the immeasurability of it and thoroughly investigates the\
disquieting elements that are involved in all the conditioned states of \
being.\
The Bodhisattva ultimately provides the suffering creatures with\
ten mental (or intellectual) dispositions, viz.(1) that what serves as the \
refuge for the deliverance of the helpless, (2) of the poor; (3) of those \
scorched by the fire of longing, loathing, and delusion; (4) of those\
confined within the prison of worldy existence; (5) of those subjected \
to hypnosis of evil passions; (6) of those incalable of discrimination; \
(7) of those destitute of good resolve, (8) of those deprived of Buddha\'92s\
discipline; (9) of those subjected to the cycle of transmigration; and \
(10) of those deprived of the means of emancipation.\{1....sattv\uc0\u257 n\u257 m antike da\u347 a citt\u257 \u347 ay\u257 n upasth\u257 payati...yad uta an\u257 th\u257 -\
tr\uc0\u257 \u7751 \u257 prati\u347 ara\u7751 acitt\u257 \u347 ayat\u257 \u7747  ca nityadaridraprati\u347 ara\u7751 acitt\u257 \u347 ayat\u257 \u7747  ca\

He perceives that the sentient beings are confronted with endless \
disconfroting factors.He calls up his dormant energy and becomes \
aware of the fact that the responsibility of providing them with speedy \
relief rests with him. He ponders upon the ways and means calcu-\

speech, (-v\uc0\u257 c) right conduct (-karm\u257 nta), \{2.Suzuki, MB, 317.\} right means of livelihood (-\u257 j\u299 va\
right effort -vy\uc0\u257 y\u257 ma), right recollection (-sm\u7771 ti), and right mystic trance\
(sam\uc0\u257 dhi) \{4.Ibid, 24.\}\
His attachments pertaining to \uc0\u257 tman, sattva, j\u299 va, po\u7779 a, pudgala\
skandha, dh\uc0\u257 tu, and \u257 yatana which are preceded by his heretical\
notion of the existence of a real physical body come to a complete\
extinction.His mind reaches an ideal state of perfection due to the\
development of its different sterling qualities.He acquires the pre-\
dominance of energy qua virtue of perfection and of sam\uc0\u257 n\u257 rthata as one\
of the four articles of gathering (sa\uc0\u7747 grahavastu).\
5.The sudurjay\uc0\u257 \
An aspirant for the blessed status of a Boddhisattva continues his\
progress without relenting his sedulous effort even for a moment.He \
lands on the fifth stage called sudurjay\uc0\u257 , and this significant name is \
indicative of the fact that it is immensely difficult to achieve victory\
over it.\{5.Cf. sattv\uc0\u257 n\u257 m parip\u257 ka\u347 ca avacittasya ca rak\u7779 a\u7751 \u257  |\
dh\uc0\u299 madbhir j\u299 yate du:kha\u7747  durjay\u257  tena kathayate ||\
s\uc0\u363 tr\u257 l.XXI.35\} He dwells in this stage and develops ten equalities of pure\
mental dispositions (citt\uc0\u257 \u347 ayavi\u347 uddhisamat\u257 )\{6.This technical term and the ten varities of it admit of different interpretations.\} They may be enumerated \
in the following order : equality of pure mental disposition relative to \
(1) the past, (2) present and (3) future Buddha-dharma, (4) morality, \
(5) thought or resolution, (6) elimination of heresy, doubt, \
perplexity or mental disturbance, (7) knowledge of noble or evil path,\
(8) knowedge of religious exertion concerning approved course of \
conduct, (9) more and superior realivation of all dharmas that are\
helpful to the attainment of enlightenment, and (10) the act of bringing\
all creatures to maturity.\{7.\'85 sa da\uc0\u347 abhi\u347  citt\u257 sayavi\u347 uddhisamat\u257 bhir avatarati\'85 at\u299 tabuddh\u257 -\
dharmavi\uc0\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 ayasamatay\u257 ca, an\u257 gatabuddhadharmavi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 aya-\
samatay\uc0\u257  ca\'85 pratyupannabuddhabdharmavi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 yasamatay\u257  ca, \
\uc0\u347 \u299 lavi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 ayasamatay\u257  ca, cittavi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 ayasamatay\u257  ca, d\u7771 \u7779 \u7789 i-\
k\uc0\u257 \u7751 k\u7779 \u257 vimativilekh\u257 panayanavi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 ayasamatay\u257  ca m\u257 rg\u257 m\u257 rga-\
j\'f1\uc0\u257 navi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 ayasamatay\u257  ca pratipatprah\u257 \u7751 aj\'f1\u257 navi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 ayasama-\
tay\uc0\u257  ca, sarvabodhipak\u7779 yadharmottarottaravibh\u257 vanavi\u347 uddhy\u257 \u347 ayasama-\

@013\
He comprehends the four noble truths (\uc0\u257 rya-satya), viz.sorrow\
(du:kha), the cause of sorrow (du:kha-samuday\uc0\u257 ), annihilation of sorrow\
(du:kha-nirodha), and the course of conduct or the way leading to the\
annihilation of sorrow (du:kha-nirodhag\uc0\u257 min\u299  pratipat) in their true \
nature.He becomes coversant and enlightened with different types of \
truth, viz. (1) sa\uc0\u7747 v\u7771 ti-satya, (2) param\u257 rtha- (3) lak\u7779 a\u7751 a-, (4) vibh\u257 ga-, \
(5) nist\uc0\u299 ra\u7751 a-, (6) vastu-, (7) prabh\u257 va-, (8) k\u7779 ay\u257 nutp\u257 da-,\
(9) m\uc0\u257 rgaj\'f1\u257 n\u257 vat\u257 ra-, (10) tath\u257 gata-j\'f1\u257 na-samudaya- and the like.\{1.An explanation of these term has been furnished in the DBHS, 27.\}\
He realizes that all conditioned states of being are void and \
illusory.His great compassion for all sentient beings increases in\
intensity.Upon him dawn the light of infinite love. \{2.tasya bh\uc0\u363 yasy\u257  m\u257 tray\u257  sattve\u7779 u mah\u257 karu\u7751 \u257  abhimukhibhavati mah\u257 -\
maitry\uc0\u257 loka\u347  ca pr\u257 durbhavati- Ibid, 27.\} He becomes \
conscious of the fact that all creatures are bereft of the soul as the\
basis of individuality and what is attributed to it as its functions.\
He laments over the moral and spiritual retrogression and endless \
sufferings of those who are chiefly engrossed in the temporal concerns \
of life. Provided with the enlightenment, he plants the roots of merit\
that pave the way to the attainment of universal emancipation.\
A nascent Bodhisattva who stays in this fifth stage develops\
his mental, intellectual, and moral qualities by meticulous observance \
of rigorous course of discipline and ceaseless application. His all-round \
elevation enables him to fulfil his mission of bringing about spiritual \
regeneration of all beings.\
He brings all creatures to a state of maturity by means of \
charity, amiable speech, instructions on the Doctrine, unfoldment\
of the faults of worldly existence, performance of magical feats\
and exhibition of supernatural powers.He achieves mastery\
of the different branches of popular science and literature which\
reveal the infaiible ways that lead to the material welfare and\
happiness of all creatures.Bisides his roots of merit come to be\
@014\
reinforced by expedients and wisdom, and attain higher and higher\
degree of splendour and refinement.His mystic trance qua virtue of \
perfection gains preponderance in this realm.He gets a direct vision \
of truth.\
6.The abhimukh\uc0\u299 \
A future Bodhisattva ultimately conquers the fifth stage and \
succeeds to enter into the succeeding one that goes under the name of\
abhimukh\uc0\u299 .It is characterized by the predominance of trans-\
cendental wisdom (praj\'f1\uc0\u257 ) \{1.Cf.abhimukhy\u257 d dvayasye\'92ch sa\u7747 s\u257 rasy\u257 \'92pi nirv\u7771 te: | \
ukta hy abhimukhi bh\uc0\u363 m\u299 : praj\'f1\u257 p\u257 ramit\u257 \u347 ray\u257 t || s\u363 tral.XXI.36\}.HE treads on this realm by reflecting \
upon the ten varieties of equality or sameness of nature of all \
states of being (dharma), viz.absence of cause, of distinctive charac-\
teristic, of origination and the like. \{2.\'85 sa da\uc0\u347 abhir dharmasat\u257 bhir avatarati, \'85 yad uta sarvadharm\u257 ni-\
mittasamatay\uc0\u257  ca sarvadharmalak\u7779 a\u7751 asamatay\u257  ca sarvadharm\u257 nutp\u257 -\
dasamatay\uc0\u257  ca sarvadharm\u257 j\u257 tatay\u257  ca\'85 DBHS, 31\} He attains to intellectual \
receptivity which is conducive to reflection on the states of being\
(\uc0\u257 nulomik\u299  k\u7779 \u257 nti).But he is not spiritually prepared to reach the\
threshold of the receptivity that concerns itself with the fact that they \
(states of being) are bereft of production (anutpattika-dharma-k\uc0\u7779 \u257 nti) \{3.\'85 na ca t\u257 vad anutpattikadharmak\u7779 \u257 ntimukham anupr\u257 pnoti\'85 Ibid, \
31.Cf.also BHS, 27.\} \
When he realizes them in their true light, he reflects on the origination \
and destruction of beings with increased concentration.His mind\
becomes saturated with love and compassion for them.He understands\
the profound truth that all wordly activities and behaviours owe their\
existence to adherence to the heretical notion of the self as a real \
exitent.And he finds access into the truth that the cessation of the\
latter entails the cessation of the former. \{4.\'85y\uc0\u257 vatyo lokasamud\u257 s\u257 ropapattaya: sarv\u257 : t\u257  \u257 tm\u257 bhinive\u347 ato\
bhavanti.\uc0\u257 tmabhinive\u347 avigamato na bhavanti lokasamud\u257 c\u257 ropa-\
pattaya: \'85Ibid, 31\} \
A deeper thought unfolds the mystery to him that there \
is the darkness of ignorance which envelops the light of \
enlightenment and allures all sentient beings to swerve from \
the path of truth.He comprehends that an ignorant individual piles \
up accumulations of Karman which are meritorious, demertorious and\
productive of immobile conditions.\{5.BHS, 57\} These accumulations ultimately \
@015\
pave the way for sowing the seeds of consciousness associated with\
depravities and addiction to existence. And as a sequel to it these\
seeds of consciousness become attended with the states of birth (j\uc0\u257 ti)\
senility, death, and rebirth.His field of Karman in which the seeds are \
sown is a habitation and is veiled by the gloom of ignorance.The \
moisture of craving moistens them; and the water of personal vanity\
irrigates them; and gradual expansion of the network of heretical\
views offers an opportunity for the sprouting of name and from.\{1.DBHS, 31\}\
From name and form are produced the five sence-organs.\
And from the co-association of the five sense-organs are produced \
contacts with sense-objects.From the contacts are produced \
sensations. From sensation are produced longings.From longing\
is produced increased clinging.And from the growth of clinging\
are produced the states of existence. From the states of existence\
is produced a body or personality constituted of five\
conglomerations, viz. from (r\uc0\u363 pa), sensation, (vedan\u257 ), notions or \
conceptions (sa\uc0\u7747 j\'f1\u257 ), accumulated predispositions (sa\u7747 sk\u257 ra) and \
individuated consciousness (vij\'f1\uc0\u257 na)\
To him it is revealed that conscious beings become contaminated \
owing to their association with the five order of existence, viz.hell, \
lower animals, departed sprits, deities, and human beings.This contami-\
nation produces mental fever and fever-heat.And they in their turn\
become the cause of all mental pain, incoherent prattle, sorrow, dejection, \
and mental disturbance, A Bodhisattva-to-be profoundly reflects (2. \'85eva\uc0\u7747  bodhisattavo\'92nulom\u257 k\u257 ra\u7747  pratiyasamutp\u257 da\u7747  pratyavek\u7779 ate.\
Ibid.\} on this\
concatenated process of origination of the effect in dependence on the\
antecedent condition (pratiyasamutp\uc0\u257 da), and realizes that there is no\
savior of mankind from this lamentable condition.\
He ponders over the two distinct functions of the twelve links\
constituting the chain of dependent origination.He discovers that\
ignorance engenders delusion by providing the objects of sense-organs.\
Over and above it operates as the cause that brings about the\
accomplishment of sa\uc0\u7747 sk\u257 ra.\{3.Ibid, 32.\} Likewise he finds out that a two-fold \
function which belongs to each succeeding link differs in each\
case.To him it becomes unfolded that the twelve links (members, \
@016\
conditions) of the state of existence are of the nature of three states \
of pain, viz.(1) state of pain occasioned by conditioning (sa\uc0\u7747 sk\u257 ra-\
du:khat\uc0\u257 ), (2) state of pain qua pain (du:khadu:khat\u257 ) and (3) state\
of pain occasioned by constant fluxion (pari\uc0\u7751 \u257 madu:khat\u257 ).He\
incessantly contemplates on the essential nature of the twelve-link\
dependent origination from different respects and aspects.\{1.DBHS, 32\} And as a\
consequence of it, there emerge into existence the three entrances to \
(or threshold of) spiritual liberation (vimok\uc0\u7779 a-mukha), viz. (1) \u347 \u363 nyat\u257 -\
vimok\uc0\u7779 a-mukha, (2) \u257 nimitta-, and (3) apra\u7751 ihita- \{2.Ibid, 33-4.\}\
He undertakes strenuous relogios exercises for the accomplish-\
ment of those constitutive members of enlightenment (bodhya\uc0\u7749 ga) which\
remain to be accomplished.Furthermore, he clearly comprehends\
the reasons which are responsible for the production and cessation of \
the conditioned state of existence.He becomes conscious of the\
fact that the stage called praj\'f1\uc0\u257 -p\u257 ramit\u257 -vih\u257 ra has turned \
its face towards him.He becomes engrossed in the mystic\
contemplation pertaining to voidity of endless varieties.He\
also feels that a thousand entrances to the three mystic\
contemplations, viz. \uc0\u347 \u363 nyat\u257 , \u257 nimitta, and apra\u7751 ihita are drawing\
nearer to the state of his realization.\{3.Ibid, 34\} His ten different states of\
mental disposition attain more and more perfection.His roots of \
merit attain purification to a considerable measure and the process\
extends over innumerable kalpas without any break or interregnum\{4.Ibid, 35\}.\
His tactfulness concerning expedients, intelligence and knowledge\
impart more and more transparency to them (roots of merit).They\
extinguish the flame of sorrows and sufferings of endless crores of \
creatures and comfort them with delight like the serene moon-light.\
They remain beyond the sphere of the four realms of m\uc0\u257 ra.His\
perfect virtue of knowledge (praj\'f1\uc0\u257 p\u257 ramit\u257 ) gains primacy in this\
domain.\
7.The d\uc0\u363 ra\u7749 gam\u257 \
A progressive Bodhisattava wins stage after stage.His increasing\
religious and spiritual ardour urges him to continue his onwards march\
and sustains him steady in order to conquer the seventh stage called\
@017\
d\uc0\u363 ra\u7749 gam\u257 \{1.Cf. ek\u257 yanapatha\u347 le\u7779 \u257 d bh\u363 mir dura\u7749 gam\u257  mat\u257 .\
s\uc0\u363 tral.XXI.37\}. He is provided with intelligence, knowledge, and skill\
in devices conducive to the effectuation of ten beginnings of a new way.\{2.De La vallee-poussin, Bodhisattva,-ERE, 747; cf. sa da\uc0\u347 abhir up\u257 ya-\
praj\'f1\uc0\u257 -j\'f1\u257 n\u257 bhinirh\u7771 tair m\u257 rg\u257 ntar\u257 rambhavi\u347 c\u7779 air \u257 kramati.katamair\
da\uc0\u347 abhi: ? yad uta \u347 \u363 nyat\u257 nimitt\u257 pra\u7751 ihitasam\u257 dhisuparibh\u257 vita-\
m\uc0\u257 nasa\u347  ca bhavati, ...et seq.DBHS, 36.\} \
And it is intended for spiritual emancipation of the mass of creatures.\
His mind reaches an ideal state of rarefication due to the ceaseless \
practice of three mystic contemplations, viz. \uc0\u347 \u363 nyat\u257 , \u257 nimitta and\
apra\uc0\u7751 ihita.He acquires and augments the quantum of merit and\

the ultimate end of his life.He comprehends that all states of \
existence and the so-called things are devoid of ego and essence.\
There is no such entity as individualbeing or creature.He never\
forsakes the four brahmavih\uc0\u257 ras, viz. maitr\u299 , karu\u7751 \u257 , mudit\u257 , and\
upek\uc0\u7779 \u257 .\
He refrains from adhering to or entering into any Other dharma.\
He realizes the intrinsic difference of the triple world, viz.the world of \
desire (k\uc0\u257 ma-dh\u257 tu), the world of from (r\u363 pa-), and the world of the from-\
less (\uc0\u257 r\u363 pyadh\u257 tu).His renunciation of the fleeting temporal affairs is not \
inspired by egocentric interest.\{3.DBHS, 36.\} He succeeds in extinguishing the flames of \
passion and affictions. He dedicates himself to the task of bringing\
about the deliverance of the vulgar masses from the blazing fire of long-\
ing and loathing.He is perfectly persuaded that all states of existence \
are mere phantom.He is conscious of the fact that they are bereft \
of reality and bear resemblance to the illusion (m\uc0\u257 y\u257 ), mirage, echo, \
dream-experience and the image of the moon reflected in the water.\{4.Ibid, 36.\}\
A Bodhisattva who abides in this stage becomes provided with \
the comprehension of infiniteness relative to the (1) number and classes \
of creatures, (2) modes of feligious training imparted by the Buddhas, \
(3) world-spheres, (4) purification of the land of the Buddhas, (5) states \
of existence, (6) supernatural knowledge, and (7) assumption of material\
forms, utterance of voice, and deliverance of sermons by the Buddhas \
including their instruction on the threshold of Buddha-knowledge.\
@018\
He holds fast to appropriate behavior (\uc0\u299 ry\u257 p\u257 tha). He practises\
the ten virtues of perfection (p\uc0\u257 ramit\u257 ) withaout abreak even for a\
moment.They are charity (d\uc0\u257 na), morality (\u347 \u299 la), receptivity or patience\
(k\uc0\u7779 \u257 nti), energy (v\u299 rya), mystic trance (dhy\u257 na), intelligence (praj\'f1\u257 )),\
adeptness in expendient (up\uc0\u257 yakau\u347 ala), vow (pra\u7751 idh\u257 na), power (bala)\
and authentic knowledge (j\'f1\uc0\u257 na).Besides, he cultivates and fulfils\
the four articles of gathering (sa\uc0\u7747 grahavastu), viz. d\u257 na, priya-vacana, \
artha-kriy\uc0\u257  (or cary\u257 ), and sam\u257 n\u257 rthat\u257 ; the four adhi\u7779 \u7789 h\u257 nas, \
viz. satya, ty\uc0\u257 ga, upa\u347 ama, and praj\'f1\u257 ; thirty-seven virtues conducive\
to the attainment of enlightenment; and three thresholds of \
spiritual liberation, viz. \uc0\u347 \u363 nyat\u257 , \u257 nimitta, and apra\u7751 ihita.\{1.eva\u7747  catv\u257 ri sa\u7747 grahavast\u363 ni parip\u363 ryante, catv\u257 ri ca adhi\u7779 \u7789 h\u257 n\u257 ni, \
saptatri\uc0\u7747 \u347 ad bodhipak\u7779 y\u257 s ca dharm\u257 :, tr\u299 \u7751 i ca vimok\u7779 amukh\u257 ni\
\'85parip\uc0\u363 rayante, DBHS, 37.\} His adept-\
ness in expedients qua virtue of perfection gains supremacy in this stage.\{2.Ibid, 41.\}\
8. The acal\uc0\u257 \
A future Bodhisattva is approaching nearer and nearer the\
\'91ultimate goal of his life.His indefatigable energy enable him to pass \
from the seventh to the eight stage that bears the name of achal\uc0\u257 \{3.dvayasa\u7747 j\'f1\u257 vicalan\u257 d acal\u257  ca nirucyate |\
s\uc0\u363 tral, XXI.37.\} and\
is characterized by the distinctive traits of its own.It signifies that \
in the career of the Bodhisattva, this stage in progressive spiritual \
realization is immovable and as such precludes the possibility of \
retrogression.\{4.The DBHS has stated that the eighth bodhisattvabh\uc0\u363 mi receives the\
following designation, viz. avivartya, d\uc0\u363 r\u257 sada, kum\u257 ra, janma, parini\u7779 panna, \
parini\uc0\u7779 \u7789 hita, nirm\u257 \u7751 a (nirv\u257 \u7751 a), adhi\u7779 \u7789 hi\u257 na and an\u257 bhoga.\} A candidate for Bodhisattvahood who succeeds to enter\
into it by discarding false discriminations becomes endowed with an \
exalted state of realization\{5.\'85 avat\uc0\u299 r\u7751 onutpattikadharmak\u7779 \u257 ntipr\u257 pta ityucyate- DBHS, 42.\} called anutpattika-dharma-k\u7779 \u257 nti.\{6.Different explanations of this omportant technical term may be set forth\
in the following order :\
(i) intellectual receptivity to the truth that states of existence have no origina-\
tion (BHS, 27)\
(ii) Upholding the doctrine of the non-prodution of things (De La Valler-\
Pousain, Bodhisattva)\
(iii) not created being for bearance (Suzuki).\} He\
becomes exempted from all efforts and attains a state of effortlessness.\
@019\
This blessed state has been portrayed by resorting to an apt simile.\
An individual in his dream makes frantic efforts to cross a vast sheet\
of flood-water.Ultimately his dream is broken and his activities are \
brought to a cessation.In an indentical way a bodhisattva becomes \
apparently conscious of the fact that all unenlightened beings are under\
the sway of four ogh\uc0\u257 s\{1.Cf. \u257 sravas\} and as such he undertakes a rescue operation.\
But immediately after the attainment of this stage, he realizes the \
futility of all his efforts\{2.tad yath\uc0\u257  pi n\u257 ma\'85 puru\u7779 a: sputa: svapn\u257 ntaragato mahaugha-\
pr\uc0\u257 ptam \u257 tm\u257 na\u7747  sa\u7747 j\u257 n\u299 t..samanantaram anupr\u257 pta im\u257 m acal\u257 \u7747 \
bodhisattvabh\uc0\u363 mi\u7747  sarv\u257 bhogavigato bhavati.-DBHS, 42\} and all his previous spiritual preparations\
become deprived of their significance.He reached the preceding seven \
stages by relentless endeavour.But in the stage under review all \
his activities are automatic.He does not feel the necessity of \
observing the different varieties of samud\uc0\u257 caras  relating to the Buddhas, \
the Bodhisattvas, nirv\uc0\u257 \u7751 a and the Arhats.\
The Blessed Buddhas provide tath\uc0\u257 gata- enlightenment to him \
and declare that his receptivity to (patience in) the supreme truth\
is conducive to the way for the realization of the Doctrine of the\
Buddha and they heap praises upon him.But they remind him that \
he has not yet attained the ten powers (bala) and the four confidences\
(vai\uc0\u347 \u257 radya).They exhort him to strive after the achievement of the\
wealth of Buddha\'92s Doctrine.Besides, they urge him to pay heed to \
the wretched codition of the ignorant laics who are grofaning under\
different varieties of affiction and whose minds are under the hypnotic\
spell of false discriminations.\
They bid him behold their infinite bodies, infinite knowledge, \
infinite kingdoms, infinite accomplishment pertaining to knoweledge, \
infinite immaculacy of voices and limbs.They urge him to bring \
those infinite qualities into a state of accomplishment within himself.\
Before the attainment of this stage the Bodhisattva-to-be was \
associated with a single and solitary body and with it he pursued the \
course of the conduct of Bodhisattvas.\{3.\'85 p\uc0\u363 rvam ekak\u257 y\u257 bhinih\u257 ratay\u257  cary\u257 bhinirh\u257 ro\'92bh\u363 t.im\u257 \u7747  punar-\
bh\uc0\u363 m\u299 \u7747  sam\u257 r\u363 \u7693 hasya bodhisattvasya apram\u257 \u7751 ak\u257 yavibhaktito bodhi-\
sattvacary\uc0\u257 bala\u7747  samud\u257 gacchati- Ibid, 43.\} But now he splits up his body \
into infinite fromd and thereby attains the power styled bodhisattva-\
@020\
cary\uc0\u257 .In this stage all his spiritual attainmenta are without any \
limitation.It is due to the dawning of his omniscience that he is \
in a position to know the entire universe.\
Even after the attainment of the stage called the Immovable, the\
Bodhisattva is not entitled to enter nirv\uc0\u257 \u7751 a.Since this would bring\
about a termination of all activities directed towards redemption of all \
creatures.It is owing to this reason that the Bodhisattva refrains \
from entering into the state of nirv\uc0\u257 \u7751 a and elects to continue his\
worldly existence.But the activities of his body, voice and mind \
come to a comlete cessation.The functioning of his previous vows \
takes place without encountering any hitch and his spiritual progress\
reaches the pattern of perfection.\
A Bodhisattva firmly entrenched in this stage achieves ten \
masteries (va\uc0\u347 it\u257 ), viz. \u257 yura-va\u347 it\u257 , ceto-va, pari\u7779 k\u257 ra-, karma-upapatti-, \
adhimukti-, and the like.\{1.DBHS, 46.\}  Furthermore, he acquires the ten balas, viz.\
\uc0\u257 \u347 aya-bala, adhy\u257 \u347 aya-bala, mah\u257 karu\u7751 \u257 -bala, and so forth and so on.\{2.Ibid.\}\
It is worthy of note that he develops the virtue of perfection of \
earnest resolution (pr\uc0\u257 \u7751 idh\u257 na-p\u257 ramit\u257 .).\{3.Ibid, 48.\}\
9.The s\uc0\u257 dhumat\u299 \
A future Bodhisattva keeps up his hazardous journey and there\
is no room for complacency in his mind.He reaches the ninth stage\
called s\uc0\u257 dhumat\u299  which is permeated with gooddness.A bodhisattva\
who resides in it succeeds to realize the accomplishment of the different\
varieties of dharma, viz.meritoious, demeritorious, indeterminate, pure, \
impure, mundane, supramundane, conditioned and unconditioned \{4.uddha\'92s doctrine is regarded as unconditioned (asa\uc0\u7747 sk\u7771 ta).\} in \
their true light \{5.s\uc0\u257 dhumaty\u257 \u7747  bodhisattvabh\u363 mau sthit\u257 : ku\u347 al\u257 ku\u347 al\u257 vyak\u7771 tadharm\u257 -\
bodhisattvabh\uc0\u363 ta\u7747  praj\u257 n\u257 ti\'85et seq.\'96Ibid, 49\} He acquires the knowledge of the doctrines pertaining\
to the vehicle of the \uc0\u347 r\u257 vakas, Pratyekabuddhas, Bodhisattvas and the\
tath\uc0\u257 gata.He delivers the message of Buddha\'92s doctrine to all\
sentient beings.To him becomes revealed the endless diversity of \
psychical faculties of all creatures.\{6.sa sattv\uc0\u257 n\u257 \u7747  cittavaim\u257 trat\u257 \u7747  ca\'85 yath\u257 bh\u363 ta\u7747  praj\u257 n\u257 ti -Ibid, 49\}\
@021\
He attains four-fold special knowledge (pratisa\uc0\u7747 vid), viz. (1)\
dharmapratisa\uc0\u7747 vid, (2) artha-, (3) nirukti-, and (4) pratibh\u257 na-.\{1.It is remarkable that the utility of these pratisa\u7747 vids has been elaborately\
exhibited in different ways the author of the da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mika-s\u363 tra.We \
may quote a relevant portion of it in order to indicate the mode of their\
development : sa dharmapratisa\uc0\u7747 vid\u257  svalak\u7779 a\u7751 a\u7747  dharm\u257 \u7751 \u257 m praj\u257 n\u257 ti.\
arthapratisa\uc0\u7747 vid\u257  vibhakti\u7747  dharm\u257 \u7751 \u257 m praj\u257 n\u257 ti.niruktipratisa\u7747 vid\u257 \
asa\uc0\u7747 bhedade\u347 an\u257 \u7747  dharm\u257 \u7751 \u257 \u7747  praj\u257 n\u257 ti.pratibh\u257 napratisa\u7747 vid\u257  anu-\
prabhandh\uc0\u257 nupacchesat\u257 \u7747  dharm\u257 \u7751 \u257 m praj\u257 n\u257 ti- DBHS, 51 Cf.also\
pratisa\uc0\u7747 vinmatis\u257 dhutv\u257 d bh\u363 mi (1a) s\u257 dhumati mat\u257 , sutral, XXI.38; \
Ia p\uc0\u257 da hypermetre (l\u363 vi).\} his \
will transcends all limitations. What he wills is brought into actual\
realization.\{2.DBHS, 52-53.\} His acquirement of supernatural power qua virtue of \
perfection is preponderant in this realm.\{3.Ibid, 54.\}\
10.The dharmamegh\uc0\u257 \
The aspirant who seeks after the sublimest status of Bodhisattva-\
hood now reaches the end of his quest.He mounts upon the summit.\
He ascends the highest rung of the ladder of bodhisattva-bh\uc0\u363 mi.\
His tenth and the final stage of progressive spiritual realization receives \
the significant designation of dharmamegh\uc0\u257  or Cloud of the Doctrine.\{4.It has also received the names of abhi\u7779 ekabh\u363 mi (stage of holy consecration)\
and the like-Ibid, 55.\}\
He becomes entitled to realize innumerable varicties of contemplations \
including the ten unique types of them.\{5.These ten sam\uc0\u257 dhis have been enumerated in the following order, viz.\
(1) vimala, (2 dharmadh\uc0\u257 tuvibhaktiprave\u347 a, (3) bodhima\u7751 \u7693 ala\u7747 k\u257 ravyuha,\
(4) sarv\uc0\u257 k\u257 ra\u347 mikusuma, (5) s\u257 garagarbha, (6) s\u257 garasam\u7771 ddhi, (7) \u257 k\u257 \u347 adh\u257 tu-\
vipula, (8) sarvadharmasvabh\uc0\u257 vavicaya, (9) sarvasattvacittacarit\u257 nugata, (10) pratyutpannasarvabudha-sa\u7747 mukh\u257 casthitO- Ibid.\} And at the end the contem-\
plation called sarvaj\'f1\uc0\u257 navi\u347 e\u7779 \u257 bhi\u7779 eka\{6.\'85sa tasya sarvaj\'f1\u257 j\'f1\u257 navi\u347 e\u7779 \u257 bhi\u7779 ekavata: sam\u257 dhe: sahapratilam-\
bh\uc0\u257 t tasmin mah\u257 ratnar\u257 japadme ni\u7779 a\u7751 \u7751 a: sa\u7747 d\u7771 \u347 yate- Ibid.\
Cf....acal\uc0\u257 s\u257 dhumat\u299 dharamamegh\u257 bh\u363 mivyavasthito\'85 la\u7749 k, 7\} also becomes manifest to \
him.And as soon as this realization takes place, he is beheld to be\
seated upon a luminous seat that bears the significant name mah\uc0\u257 ratna-\
r\uc0\u257 japadma and including other ten varieties of it (seat).It emits a \
myriad of radiant rays which illuminate all the ten quarters and work \
out innumerable miracles.The Buddhas appear before him and\
consecrate him in supreme enlightenment.\
@022\
He understands the appearance of phenomenal plurality \
in its true nature.He realizes the different types of magical\
creation.He comprehends all the guhyasth\uc0\u257 nas.\{1.DBHS, 58\} He is now\
entitled to know the different varieties of attainment of entrance into \
different world-ages\{2.Ibid, 59\}.He wins the ten Bodhisattvavimok\uc0\u7779 as including\
the innumerable approaches to them \{3.Ibid.\} He endures the cloud of the\
light of the vision of the great Doctrine that goes under the name of \
the treasure of the sphere of religion pertaining to the three times.\{4.Ibid, 60\}\
He puts out the flames of affictions produced by ignorance by means\
of showering \{5.Ibid, 61\}\
the rain of great nectar of merit.\{6.It is one of the reasons that accounts for the conferment of the name of \
dharmamegh\uc0\u257  upon the stage under review.Cf. dharmamaegh\u257  dvayavy\u257 -\
pter dharm\uc0\u257 k\u257 \u347 asya meghavat-s\u363 tr\u257 l.XXI.38.,\
The yogas\uc0\u363 tra of pata\'f1jali has elucidated the essential nature of the\
spiritual contemplation called Dharmamegha in the way indicated below :\
prasa\uc0\u7747 khy\u257 ne\'92py akus\u299 dasya vivekakhy\u257 ter dharmameghassam\u257 dhi:.\
IV.29.The author of the pa\'f1cada\uc0\u347 \u299  has also made the following significant observation :\
dharmamegha\uc0\u7747  ima\u7747  pr\u257 hu: sam\u257 dhi\u7747  yogavittam\u257 : |\
var\uc0\u7779 aty e\u7779 a yato dharm\u257 m\u7771 tadh\u257 : sahasra\u347 a: || I.60.\} His will transcends\
all limitation and becomes endowed with supernatural power.\
His knowledge qua virtue of perfection becomes predominant in this\
final realm.\{7.DBHS, 64\}\
Before concluding our succinct survey of the ten bodhisattva-\
bh\uc0\u363 mis, I think it necessary to make en passant a few pertinent\
observations.The old yog\uc0\u257 c\u257 ra school, sponsored by maitreyan\u257 tha, \
asa\uc0\u7749 ga and Vasumandhu is definitely committed to the view that\
\uc0\u347 \u363 nyat\u257  is the assessment of the phenomenal world as pure appearance.\
One reality, dharmak\uc0\u257 ya, pervades the entire reality.It is one and\
same in all consciousness-centres.The dharmak\uc0\u257 ya is conscious, pure\
and simple, and is the equivalent of the upani\uc0\u7779 adic bhahman as\
interpreted by gau\uc0\u7693 ap\u257 da and \u347 a\u7749 kar\u257 c\u257 rya.The terminology is \
only different.The buddhahood is immanent and has to be deve-\
loped and made manifest by expelling ognorance and its satellites.\
@023\
The nirodha or cessation of consciousness spoken of in this work\
and elsewhere is not cessation of pure consciousness, which is not \
liable to origin, decay or death, but of the personalized consciousness \
appearing as the ego.The nair\uc0\u257 tmya means the unreality of the ego and \
ego-centric consciousness.The mah\uc0\u257 y\u257 na Buddhist are in perfect \
unison with the advocates of the lower vehicle that there is no soul.\
But the denial of the sonl is not tantamount to universal nothingness, \
but the denial of the egoity which divides sentient creatures from \
one another and spells feud, hostility, malice and jealousy.It is \
this egoity which brings about war.There is no `I\'92 or to be precise, \
no plural `Is\'92. \uc0\u347 \u363 nyat\u257  Is to be understood as the \u347 \u363 nyat\u257  (unreality)\
of the personal identity of the subject and of the objective world.\
The subject as the ego must disappear and with it the object.The\
vij\'f1\uc0\u257 na in the  prat\u299 tyasamutp\u257 da cycle is the personalized, polluted\
and imperfect manifestation of the dharmak\uc0\u257 ya.The personalized\
consciousness is only a distortion of it.\
The ethics of Bodhisattvahood is a marvel and by its universal\
appeal is bound to capture the hearts of all unprejudiced persons.\
To be self-centered is to be entangled in misery and the identification \
of oneself with all is the secret of emancipation.So long as Buddhism \
remained true to this ideal of one Buddhahood immanent in all and \
transcending all limits, it was a power which could not be vanquished.\
When it swerved from this ideal, it became weak and was supplanted\
by Islam and Christianity.These later religions won adherents from the\
Buddhist laity and the same process is still at work in the Buddhist\
countries of South East Asia.Buddhism is not the sdvocate of the\
brotherhood of Buddhists alone, but of men, gods and brutes alike.The\
world requires a synthesis of the upni\uc0\u7779 adic brahman with the active\
altruism of the Bodhisattva and the nearer and nearerwe approach this\
goal, the world will grow from good to better.\
SITANSUSEKHAR BAGCHI,\
Director, \
Mithila Research Institute, \
Darbhanga.\

@069\
da\uc0\u347 a\{1. The DBh consists of two sections, one in prose, edited by\
Dr. Johannes Rahder in Roman script and published in Paris in\
1926; and the second in prose edited by Dr. J.Rahder and S.Susa,\
and published in Eastern Buddhist, Vols. V and VI, 1929-31.\
These g\uc0\u257 th\u257 s #are divided into two groups, one initial and the other\
final. This arrangement seems to be similar to the same of the\
other Buddhist s\uc0\u363 tras, introducing as well as summarizing the \
subject-matter treated. It should be noted, however, that initial or\
introductory stanzas are not usual in these sutras though the concl\
uding ones are, and hence I am inclined to believe that the g\uc0\u257 t\u257 -\
portion of the Da\uc0\u347 abh\u363 mikas\u363 tra is a positively late addition. Perhaps\
the other one also is equally late.\} bh\uc0\u363 mikas\u363 tre g\u257 th\u257 vibh\u257 ga: |\

11 par\uc0\u299 ndan\u257 parivarta: |\
upakrama: |\
et\uc0\u257 st\u257 : khalu punarbho jinaputr\u257  da\u347 a bodhisattvabh\u363 maya: sam\u257 sato nirdi\u7779 \u7789 \u257 : sarv\u257 -\
k\uc0\u257 ravaropetasarvaj\'f1aj\'f1\u257 n\u257 nugat\u257  dra\u7779 \u7789 avy\u257 : | tasy\u257 \u7747  vel\u257 y\u257 maya\u7747  tris\u257 hasramah\u257 s\u257 hasro lokadh\u257 tu: \
\uc0\u7779 a\u7693 vik\u257 ra\u7747  pr\u257 kampat | vividh\u257 ni ca pu\u7779 p\u257 \u7751 i viyato nyapatan | divyam\u257 nu\u7779 yak\u257 ni ca\
t\uc0\u363 ry\u257 \u7751 i sa\u7747 prav\u257 dit\u257 nyabh\u363 van | anumodan\u257 \u347 abdena ca y\u257 vadakani\u7779 \u7789 habhuvana\u7747  vij\'f1aptamabh\u363 t ||\
atha tasmin samaye bhagav\uc0\u257 \u7747 st\u257 n vimukticandrapramukh\u257 n sarv\u257 n bodhisattv\u257 n\u257 mantrya eva-\
m\uc0\u257 di\u347 at-im\u257 maha\u7747  m\u257 r\u7779 \u257  asa\u7747 khyeyakalpako\u7789 \u299 nayuta\u347 atasahasrasamud\u257 n\u299 t\u257 manuttar\u257 \u7747  samyaksa\u7747 bodhi\u7747 \
